               \n                    Brett Callwood                \n            \n                                    Much as Neil Young became the elder statesman of choice for the grunge generation in the 90s, Jackson Browne has become the geezer to be worshipped by fans of the modern singer-songwriter. The Los Angeles native has been blending rock, folk and country since his 1972 self-titled debut, which featured friends as prestigious as David Crosby, Graham Nash and Albert Lee. He put out three more albums in the next four years, and its the last of those, 1976s The Pretender, that shot Browne up the fame ladder, thanks in no small part to the title track. Nowadays, every folky, country-infused indie band with any modicum of hipster appeal cites Browne as an influence. Needless to say, the man has enjoyed a bit of a resurgence in recent years. His last album, 2014s Standing in the Breach, is typically thought-provoking yet hummable.
